▲ Regulations on Opium Addiction Treatment – Commander-in-Chief Chiang, considering that personnel and students in Party, government, and military services in the three provinces are addicted to opium and seem unwilling to change, has issued strict orders to quit opium within a specified time limit. He has specially stipulated measures for opium addiction treatment. On the 31st, he sent letters to the Party departments, high courts, and schools in the provinces and cities of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, ordering each pacification headquarters, provincial government, army, and division to comply. The original letter stated: [Opium is deeply poisonous. Once addicted, it erodes ambition, ruins reputation, destroys careers, and devastates the body. It is harmful in every way to individuals and society. The people of our country are drinking poison willingly, without the slightest awareness. Every time I think about this, I feel deeply pained. The personnel of our Party, government, and military services are models for the people, and our young students are the backbone of society. If they do not improve themselves and become addicted to this evil habit, it will inevitably lead to national destruction, racial extermination, and personal ruin. The Commander-in-Chief deeply knows that many social evils originate from opium. If we want to transform society and reverse the decline, we must thoroughly and quickly ban it, especially starting with personnel in Party, government, and military services and students. This is essential to set an example]. He specifically announced to the three towns of Wuhan that all Party members, officials, soldiers, and students who smoke opium or other narcotic substances must report to the Inspection Department of the Party and Government Committee within two weeks from September 2nd, in order to quit opium on time and avoid punishment. Those who fail to report within the deadline and continue to smoke will be investigated. If the investigation is confirmed, they will be shot. The implementation dates for other counties in Hubei and the provinces of Henan and Anhui will be specified in separate orders]. Attached are the measures for opium addiction treatment for personnel in Party, government, and military services and students within a specified time limit: (1) All Party members, officials, soldiers, and students who smoke opium or alternative narcotics such as Golden Pills and heroin, or inject morphine, must report to the Inspection Department of the Party and Government Committee within two weeks and fill out a voluntary form for opium addiction treatment. (2) After reporting, the Inspection Department will designate a hospital as a place for opium addiction treatment, based on the severity of the addiction, and set a time limit of 30 or 45 days to quit completely. (3) Upon the expiration of the time limit, a designated doctor will conduct an investigation. Those who have quit will be given a certificate. Those who have not quit completely will have their time limit extended by the doctor. The extension should not exceed 60 days for mild cases and 75 days for severe cases. If they still fail to quit completely after the extended deadline, they will be dismissed from their positions and expelled from the Party and school. They will also be sent to the Medical Department of the Headquarters to be forced to quit. The medical expenses will be borne by the individual. (4) Those who fail to report within two weeks and are later discovered to be smoking opium or alternative narcotics, or injecting morphine, will be shot upon confirmation of the investigation. (5) Doctors should faithfully perform their duties during the investigation. Any concealment will be severely punished. (6) These measures will be implemented in the three towns of Wuhan starting from September 2nd. The implementation dates for other counties in Hubei and the provinces of Henan and Anhui will be specified in separate orders. (August 31st)

Investigation of Embezzlement of Dike Funds by Hubei High Court 73

Wuchang District Court Handles Case Without Corruption

Liu Wenjin Returns to Custody Awaiting Trial by the District Court

Hankou Correspondent: The case of Liu Wenjin, the former accountant of the Hubei Dike Project Expenditure Management Committee, and Cha Wenqu, the manager of the local merchant Chuanjianglong Company, jointly embezzling dike funds, has been pending for over a year without resolution. This time, Zhang Nanxian secretly investigated the case and learned that the suspect Liu had been released on bail by the Wuchang District Court. He reported this to Commander-in-Chief Chiang on suspicion of illegal release. He ordered the arrest of the Chief Prosecutor of the court, Hu Shu, for interrogation by the High Court. Coincidentally, Liu Wenjin arrived to surrender. The investigation revealed that the Wuchang District Court did not appear to be corrupt. Yesterday, the High Court reported the progress of the investigation to Commander-in-Chief Chiang. The original text is as follows: [Report on the matter of reporting the progress of handling the case of Liu Wenjin's embezzlement, as reported by Li Shi’en, the Acting Chief Prosecutor of the Wuchang District Court, requesting review and forwarding. This office received an order from your office on April 2nd and April 18th, which was forwarded by the Hubei Provincial Government, regarding the investigation of the case of Liu Wenjin's embezzlement, along with eleven copies of documents and the suspect Liu Wenjin. Prosecutor Chen Zhenggang was assigned to investigate according to law. During repeated interrogations, Liu Wenjin stated that the deposits of Chuanjianglong were transferred to me by the previous accountant, Li Wenbao, and were promissory notes. I have submitted the transfer document to the Provincial Government, and there is a receipt from the General Affairs Section of the Provincial Government as proof. He also claimed that he did not embezzle over 36,000 yuan of dike funds, but only embezzled over 5,000 yuan. He sold 3,280 yuan of property to repay the embezzled funds, which he submitted to the Provincial Government. There is a receipt from the Judicial Section of the Public Security Bureau for receiving the title deeds of the land and houses. He still owed over 1,800 yuan, which he transferred to the subsequent accountant, He Zhidao, when he was detained. He also provided a receipt from the Hubei Provincial Bank and two promissory notes from the Xucheng Qianzhuang, totaling 5,631 yuan, 7 jiao, and 3 fen, which can be verified by He Zhidao's receipt. He added that his confession was evasive, and Cha Wenqu, a person involved in the case, was summoned for interrogation. The bailiff reported that Cha Wenqu had absconded with dike funds and his whereabouts were unknown. On June 27th, we sent a letter to the Hubei Provincial Government to verify whether the payment claimed by Liu Wenjin was true, and how the interest of over 22,100 yuan was embezzled, requesting a prompt reply for verification. Later, Liu Wenjin claimed that he had been detained for two years due to a one-sided accusation and requested the detention to be stopped according to law. We checked that Liu Wenjin had been in custody since April 2nd, and by June 1st, the detention period had reached two months. We applied for an extension of the detention period for two months according to Article 73, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, deducting it until August 1st. The extended period had also expired. According to Article 73, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Procedure Law, further detention would be illegal. The case was complicated, and it was not appropriate to prosecute without a reply from the Hubei Provincial Government. Therefore, on August 1st, in accordance with the provisions of Article 75, Paragraph 1 and Paragraph 2, and Article 76 of the Criminal Procedure Law, we entrusted the accused Liu Wenzhan to Chen Dinghua, the manager of Hankou Dingfeng Hardware Store, and Li Qinlian, the manager of Xintai Mining Farm, two reputable guarantors, and ordered them to pay a deposit of 1,000 yuan, with the requirement that they be available at any time. Later, on August 11th, the Hubei Provincial Government replied, only stating that it had instructed the Hubei Dike Project Expenditure Management Committee to investigate and reply, and would forward it according to the situation upon receipt. It was not until August 16th that the Hubei Provincial Government forwarded the Hubei Dike Project Expenditure Management Committee's copy, along with three attachments. With the facts now clear, we drafted an indictment on August 20th. On one hand, we limited the bail to ensure Liu Wenjin's return, and on the other hand, we organized the case file. On August 27th, we first transferred it to the Criminal Court of our court for review. Liu Wenjin was bound on August 28th and transferred to the Criminal Court for custody on August 29th. This is the situation of our office in handling the case of Liu Wenjin's embezzlement. We hereby submit this document to your office for review and forwarding to the Judicial Administration Department and the General Headquarters for Bandit Suppression in the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui. This is for public convenience. Based on this, our office first sent Prosecutor Yang Gong to the Wuchang District Court Prosecutor's Office on the 26th to review the case file of Liu Wenjin and personally consulted the prosecutor Chen Zhenggang in charge of the case. His statement was consistent with the original report. Now, after further questioning the defendant Liu Wenjin, he stated that the detention period expired on August 1st, and he submitted a request for bail and paid a deposit of 1,000 yuan, which was true. There was no solicitation of favors or spending for influence. From the situation provided by the defendant Liu Wenjin, it appears that the Wuchang District Court Prosecutor's Office did not handle this case corruptly. The defendant Liu Wenjin has now arrived and is awaiting trial by the Criminal Court of the Wuchang District Court. In addition to a separate report to the Judicial Administration Department, we hereby submit this report for your review. Respectfully submitted to Chiang, the Chairman of the Military Commission and the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui. ] (September 1st)

Jiangsu Construction Department Coordinates Provincial Highway Construction 74

Concentrating Resources for Overall Development

The Jiangsu Province highway expenditure comes mostly from the farmland tax collected by various counties to be used for road construction. The funds are managed by the county construction bureaus and are specifically used for road construction. However, over the years, the road construction in various counties has been mostly independent and not interconnected. The roads built are mostly branch lines within the counties, and the main lines connecting the traffic of various counties have not been started, so the network cannot be connected. Therefore, over four or five years, hundreds of thousands of dollars have been spent, but the roads in the province rarely have a connected and smooth effect. This spring, the Shanghai Incident led to frequent military transportation in the rear, and the counties rushed to build military roads, as urgent as sparks, showing even more that the previous road construction work was not in accordance with the meaning of prioritizing urgency. The Jiangsu Construction Department has seen this and is planning to improve, because the province's highways are an overall cause that must be planned by the province as a whole, and the major trunk lines connecting the various counties must be built first to meet the current needs, and the branch lines of the counties will not be limited to one corner, with no way to reach all directions. The department previously suggested to the provincial government that from July of the 21st year, all the road construction funds collected from the farmland tax in various counties should be turned over to the province by half and stored in special funds for the construction of major trunk road projects throughout the province. The purpose is to concentrate financial resources to develop the province's highways as a whole and remedy the past problems of fragmented and divisive branches. The case was resolved by the provincial government and implemented accordingly. The Construction Department also formulated regulations for reporting and remitting funds and table formats for weekly and monthly reports, and notified all counties to report and remit funds on schedule to meet the needs of the project. Recently, it has been heard that after the counties received the order, more than 40 counties have replied and are complying with the regulations for reporting and remitting funds. More than 10 counties have begun to submit weekly and monthly reports. It is also heard that 15 counties have remitted half of the funds collected in July to the Construction Department for verification and receipt.

They jointly united and discussed rescue methods, and issued an urgent extra from all the newspapers in Taicang, announcing the truth of the case and the rescue situation, and asked all sectors to uphold justice and provide assistance.

Important Speech by Song 83

Regarding the Japanese Seizure of Customs in Eastern Provinces

According to the National News Agency, Finance Minister Song Zi-wen issued the following statement yesterday regarding the Japanese seizure of customs in the Eastern Provinces:

[Since the customs houses in the three northeastern provinces were forcibly taken over by Japan in March of this year, not a single penny has been remitted to the central government for debt repayment. Furthermore, not only that, but also two-thirds of the bank deposits in the name of the Inspector General of Customs before Japan seized the customs houses are still in the hands of Japan or the puppet state of Manchukuo. However, the Chinese government is still trying its best to continue paying various loans and indemnities, amounting to about 13 million taels of Shanghai silver per month. Japan completely disregards the interests of bondholders, so its international credibility has begun to decline. Now, if we compare the prices of two types of loans issued by the Chinese and Japanese governments that mature at the same time, we can see the general situation. The comparison is approximately as follows:

China's 5% Rehabilitation Loan, with a term from 1913 to 1960, was priced at 62 on April 1 of this year, around the time Japan began interfering with customs in the Eastern Provinces. However, by September 1 of this year, it had increased to 68.

Japan's 6% Gold Loan, with a term from 1924 to 1959, was priced at 79 on April 1 of this year, but by September 1 of this year, it had dropped to 68 and a half.

Based on the price on September 1, the interest rate on Chinese bonds is 7.8%, while the interest rate on Japanese bonds is about 9.2%. From this, it can be seen that the value of Chinese 5% bonds is now equal to the value of Japanese 6% bonds.

Furthermore, the Japanese News Agency recently published a statistical report compiled by the Kwantung Leased Territory Government, which stated that Dalian Customs revenue increased significantly in the first half of this year. Mr. Song also made the following remarks on this:

[If the customs revenue is calculated in silver, it has decreased. According to the report of the Inspector General of Customs, the total amount of customs revenue from January 1 to June 25 of this year, before Japan seized Dalian Customs, was 6,628,348 taels, 7 mace, and 1 fen of Haikwan silver. If calculated for a full six months, the total revenue should be in the range of 6,812,000 taels of Haikwan silver. This figure is actually 253,000 taels less than the customs revenue in the first half of last year, because the total revenue of Dalian Customs in the first half of last year was 7,065,713 taels and 4 fen of Haikwan silver. However, the Japanese report uses Japanese yen to calculate and indicate the increase in customs revenue. In fact, there is no increase in customs revenue, and it only makes people aware of the sharp fall in the price of Japanese yen. A year ago, each Japanese yen was worth 49 US cents, but today it has fallen to 22 and a half US cents. This is all due to the reckless actions of the Japanese warlords in Northeast China and Shanghai. From this, it can be seen that although Japanese Foreign Minister Uchida boasts that Manchuria can look forward to peace and prosperity, in reality, Japan's forcible occupation of the area has only caused a tragic fall in its currency value and made the domestic economy even more unsustainable,] etc.

After Japan Recognizes the Puppet State, All Northeast Navigation Rights Will Be Lost 87

Changes Will Occur in the Shipping Industry

Japan has decided to recognize the Manchurian puppet organization on the 15th of this month. From then on, Chinese merchant ships sailing to the Northeast will be subject to heavy restrictions, and the navigation rights of Yingkou and Andong ports may be completely lost to Japanese merchants at that time.

▲Tonnage Tax Will Be Levied in the Northeast After the Northeast Customs was seized, China has been chanting the slogan of a blockade policy, but it has been hesitant and has not yet been realized. Since the establishment of the puppet organization, it has not been recognized internationally. Therefore, although the customs of Yingkou, Andong, and other places have been forcibly occupied, they have never dared to collect import and export taxes and ship tonnage taxes, fearing international disputes. Therefore, Chinese and foreign merchant ships can still pass as before without any obstacles. Now, Japan rashly recognizes the puppet state. Within the scope of the Northeast, the ship tax, which the customs of Andong and Yingkou had planned but dared not implement, will be levied on Japanese ships starting from September 15. Ships that do not pay tonnage tax will be prohibited from entering the port.

▲Shipping Companies Must First Sign Commercial Treaties According to regulations, the passage of ships, whether between countries or the mutual trade of merchant ships, must first have a commercial treaty. Japan and the puppet organization have already signed a secret treaty, which is known to everyone. Now that it has recognized its country, all merchant ships sailing to the Northeast, regardless of British, American, or other countries' ships, will not be allowed to enter the ports of Andong and Yingkou until a commercial treaty is signed. At present, all countries in the world have not recognized the puppet state, let alone sign a commercial treaty. Therefore, foreign ships cannot sail to the northeastern ports. Taikoo, Jardine, and other companies in this city are also discussing and investigating this matter.

▲Problems Occur with Chinese Ships Among the Chinese merchant ships sailing to the Northeast are the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Zhao Xing, Zheng Ji, Yu Da, and Hai Chang companies. After the September 18th Incident last year, Zhao Xing, Yu Da, Hai Chang, Zheng Ji, and other ships employed Japanese crew members, added puppet state flags, and burned inferior northeastern coal, so they were allowed to sail. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Tu Nan" ship planned to sail to Yingkou last month. Because the shipowner was Chinese, he sent a telegram to inquire and received a reply, stopping him from going to avoid accidents. "Tu Nan" did not dare to go. In the future, after Japan recognizes the puppet state, it is feared that the Chinese ships such as Zhao Xing and Yu Da, which are allowed to sail, will also have problems, because China is the most vigorous denier of the puppet organization.

▲Japanese Ships Dominate The Northeast navigation rights will be exclusively dominated by Japanese merchant ships after September 15. The grains, medicinal materials, soybean oil, soybeans, and other items produced in the Northeast, which are transported to Europe and the United States every year, require hundreds of thousands of tons for soybeans alone, and there are also many routes to Shantou and Xiamen in China. In the past, ships from Shanghai, both Chinese and foreign, were dispatched to load them. Now, since Chinese ships cannot go, foreign merchant ships will abandon the great shipping industry due to the issue of non-recognition. Then, the hundreds of thousands of tons of export goods every year will be transported exclusively by Japanese ships. Therefore, in the past year, Dalian, Osaka, Japan Mail Coastal Shipping, and others have added a large number of merchant ships, as if they knew there would be a September 18th Incident. Now they have all sent ships to the Northeast. The loss of the Northeast shipping industry, in terms of Chinese shipping alone, will result in a loss of at least 60 to 70 million yuan in freight every year.

Guo Cheng-en, New Director of the Central Mint, Took Office Yesterday 88

Oath Ceremony Will Be Held After Official Minting Begins

Xu Ji, the director of the Central Mint, was approved to resign. After deliberation by the State Council, Guo Cheng-en was appointed as the successor. The new director, Guo, held a handover ceremony at the auditorium of the factory yesterday (the 2nd) morning and officially took office.

▲Participants All employees of the factory, from the deputy director downwards, participated. Because it was not a formal inauguration ceremony, all the ceremonies were simple. After the ceremony, Vice Director Wei Jing-zhou gave a welcome speech on behalf of all the employees. The speech briefly stated that today is the day when the new director of the factory, Director Guo, came to the factory to take office. All the staff and workers of the factory should express their utmost welcome. Director Guo has served as the director of the Hanyang Iron Works, the director of the Shanghai Arsenal, the director of the Ordnance Department, and the director of the Lianglu Railway Bureau. He has excellent qualifications and knowledge. This time, he was ordered to come to the factory, and we are deeply grateful for his appointment. We are even more fortunate to have a good leader. Therefore, the welcome of our colleagues cannot be expressed in words. I have weak talents and hold the position of deputy director. Not only am I personally willing to do my best to assist the director, but I also hope that all colleagues in the factory will work hard for the public and live up to the long-term expectations of the factory. Then,

Guo delivered a training speech, which briefly stated: I was ordered by the National Government to come to this factory as director, and I am deeply afraid that my knowledge and experience are insufficient and that I am not up to the task. Although I have previously held engineering and mechanical positions, I have little research on the situation of minting. Fortunately, among the colleagues in this factory, there are many old classmates of my brothers who will be able to provide me with good assistance. The opening of the mint is not far away, and I have two hopes for the minting of new coins: (1) The fineness of the new coins must be accurate; (2) The minting methods should be economical. Fortunately, all the minting machines in this factory are not only the best in all mints in China, but also comparable to those in Europe and the West. It is expected that the output will be fast and the fineness will be complete in the future. At the same time, brothers also have two hopes for the colleagues in this factory: 1. Abide by the office procedures. The definition of the word "procedure" is discipline in the army, school rules in the school, and factory rules in the factory. If all colleagues and workers can earnestly listen to the instructions of superiors, then the goal of order and neatness can be achieved. 2. It is necessary to have a spirit of cooperation. If there are only a few people in this factory, such as the director, deputy director, and section chiefs, it is impossible to successfully run a factory. All colleagues and workers must sacrifice personal selfishness, be open and honest, communicate with each other, and cooperate to achieve success. The most important thing is to understand that this factory is a factory with a business nature. All colleagues should recognize this point and must not have any official habits. All political activities must be put out of mind, and we must concentrate on factory affairs in order to increase the output and improve the fineness of new coins. I have high hopes.

It is reported that Director Guo will hold a supplementary oath ceremony when the factory officially starts minting.

Dutch Refund of Boxer Indemnity Agreement 89

Signing Can Be Done When Instructions Arrive

After negotiations between the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Dutch Minister, the agreement on the refund of the Dutch Boxer Indemnity has been drafted. The agreement can be formally signed after both parties request instructions and receive them. However, the Dutch side requires that there be a way to deal with Sino-Dutch public and private loans. As for the amount of the Dutch Boxer Indemnity previously reported, according to personnel from the Customs, there is a slight error. The details are recorded as follows:

▲Signing Soon According to a person in the Shanghai diplomatic community yesterday, the Dutch Boxer Indemnity agreement is currently under instruction from both parties. Our side generally has no major problems. The agreement can only take effect after the Dutch government's instructions arrive and both parties formally sign it. However, it is not yet known whether the agreement is a refund by the Dutch side or an abandonment. When the Sino-Dutch Boxer Indemnity issue was handled by Dutch Minister Oudendijk, he was instructed by his government in October of the Republic of China's 14th year to send a note to China's Ministry of Foreign Affairs, expressing goodwill and willingness to abandon the remainder of the Dutch portion of the Boxer Indemnity and use the full amount of the funds for the purpose of governing the Yellow River waterway in China. The Netherlands may send one or two engineers and attach a supervisory committee to handle the matter. After a joint meeting of the three ministries of foreign affairs, finance, and interior affairs in our country, it was completely stalled due to the many affairs in our country. It is not yet clear whether the current agreement is a separate refund method drafted by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Dutch Minister, or whether it is still based on the previous agreement to abandon the remainder. The authorities have not clearly stated. If it is an abandonment, then the current balance is not much, which is not as good as the balance in the 14th year of the Republic of China.

▲Accurate Amount of Dutch Funds The total amount of the Dutch Boxer Indemnity and the years for repayment listed in the previous newspapers are slightly different. The accurate amount obtained by the reporter of the New Sound News Agency from the investigation of the Customs is recorded as follows. The total amount of the Boxer Indemnity of various countries is determined according to the customs taels of our country, and the total amount is 450,000,000 taels, which is approximately equivalent to 67,500,000 gold pounds. The interest rate is 4% per annum. The Dutch portion is 782,100 taels, which is approximately equivalent to 1,404,651.6 Dutch guilders, calculated at 1.796 guilders per tael. The total amount of principal and interest is estimated to be 3,066,005.289 guilders. The repayment period is 39 years, not 29 years, from 1902 to 1940. During the European War, our country joined the Allied Powers, and various countries agreed to suspend payment for five years. However, because the Netherlands did not join the Allied Powers, it did not suspend payment. Our country has always paid as usual. As of last year, a total of 2,102,957.92 guilders have been paid, and 963,047.369 guilders are still unpaid.

Page 14

▲Loan Amounts The establishment of the agreement is heard to have been expressed by the Dutch side that there must be a way to deal with Sino-Dutch public and private loans. According to the results of the New Sound News Agency's investigation by the Customs, it is known that there are only two Sino-Dutch loans. One is two transfer promissory notes from the Dutch Bank in February of the Republic of China's 7th year, totaling 427,139.76 taels of silver. By December 31 of the Republic of China's 14th year, the principal and interest had increased to 739,768.29 taels. After Yu Hede repeatedly contacted the government, it was changed to a loan. This is a private loan. The other is an amount of 17,725.89 guilders that the Dutch government took care of and paid on behalf of our country when sending back German, Austrian, and other overseas Chinese who had passed through the Netherlands in December of the Republic of China's 9th year. The interest is 89 cents. The amount should have been paid by Germany, Austria, and other countries, but because it was a time of war, our country could not contact Germany, Austria, and other countries, so it was temporarily paid by our country.

A Bomb Suddenly Exploded at Rong Chang Xiang Clock and Watch Store Last Night 90

Exploded on the Spot... Fortunately No One Was Injured

Rong Chang Xiang Clock and Watch and Glasses Store at No. 128 Fujian Road has been open for more than ten years. The owner, Wan Rong, is from Nanjing, Jiangsu Province, and is 45 years old. The manager is Wan Zhong-jie. There are a total of five employees. Someone had previously sent warning letters one week ago, but the store did not reply. Therefore, at 7:15 PM last night, someone threw a bomb. The floor at the entrance of the store was blown away by a foot. The glass cabinet and clocks and watches and glasses in the middle were all destroyed. The glass items in the cabinets on both sides were also shattered, and glass fragments were scattered all over the ground, which was very messy. The store employees were having dinner and were far away from the counter, so they were not injured. The bomber escaped. However, according to store employees in nearby stores, at around 7:00 PM, two young men dressed in short clothes resembling workers had been lingering at the entrance of the store for a long time. Later, there was a loud bang, and the two young men disappeared into the crowd.

After the Ruling of the Sanyou Factory Dispute 103

The long-delayed shutdown dispute of Sanyou Industrial Society has been formally adjudicated by the arbitration committee organized by the municipal government on the 31st of last month. The original text of the arbitral award has also been officially published. The attitudes of both parties are as follows:

▲The Labor Side Expresses Acceptance. The Seventh District Cotton Weaving Industry Association issued a notice to all sectors yesterday, saying: To all compatriots in the country, our workers of Sanyou Factory, under the unreasonable long-term announcement of shutdown by the factory, have no food or clothing, their livelihoods have been cut off, and they have groaned and wailed, calling for help repeatedly, even resorting to hunger strikes and cries of despair, in the hope of arousing the conscience of the capital side, and showing sympathy for the suffering of the workers over the years, and resuming work as soon as possible, in order to save them from their critical situation. However, it has ultimately failed to move their heart of stone. The Central People's Movement Committee, the Ministry of Industry of the National Government, and the party and government organs of this city, could not bear to see a national goods factory with a long-standing reputation suddenly shut down due to slight setbacks, plunging the future of industry into pessimism, and even more could not bear to see more than a thousand workers awaiting death, causing great panic in society. Therefore, the position of this party, the legacy of the Three Principles of the People, has repeatedly urged the resumption of work, but the capital side remains stubbornly unyielding, refusing to comply. The firmness of its attitude and the depth of its preconceptions are unprecedented in labor-capital disputes. Now this case was submitted to arbitration in the municipal government on the 31st of last month, and yesterday we read in the newspaper that it has been formally adjudicated. The main text of the award is still far from what this association had hoped for. The entire workforce, after the wailing of August, called for the full restoration of production, but now only one-fifth of it has been achieved. The pain of the matter cannot be overstated. However, this association, in view of the current national crisis and the eventful autumn in society, cannot bear to re-ignite other disturbances, giving the enemy an opportunity to take advantage of. This can be proved by reviewing the past facts. Now, although the arbitration decision has not satisfied the expectations of the workers, this association, in order to uphold the good faith mediation of the government, maintain the dignity of national laws, understand the difficulties of the capital side, and maintain the peace of the local public, is willing to sincerely and painfully accept it, in order to fulfill our people's obligation to obey the government, so that this long-delayed dispute can come to an end. From now on, we will also often order those workers who have resumed work to thoroughly implement the spirit of cooperation in the past, work together in harmony, step up production, and work together to promote the prosperity of the company's business and the development of domestic industry, in order to live up to the government's good intentions in this mediation and the kindness of the community in assisting, then the members of this association can also be comforted in the country. Sincerely, we ask for your public understanding. Shanghai Seventh District Cotton Weaving Industry Association.

▲Meal Expenses Not Received. This Wednesday (31st) was originally the date for the eleventh installment of meal expenses. The representative was helpless and withdrew. It is reported that the labor side owes Hongtai Rice Company money, but the company is demanding it very urgently, and it is difficult to cope with it for a while.

▲The Capital Side Will Have Objections. The New Voice Agency says that since the arbitration committee made the ruling, the arbitral award has been sent to the labor and capital sides. In addition to the labor side expressing reluctant agreement, the capital side believes that the arbitration decision, such as resuming a part of the work within three months, with the minimum being the capacity to accommodate one-fifth of the workers, and the remaining workers being dismissed according to the original contract, cannot be done in reality. Local News 2

Major Case of Theft and Exchange of Raw Opium in the Public Security Bureau 104

Director of the Stolen Goods Department Driven by Greed

Secretary Han Tuizhi Suspected of Involvement

Ten Thousand Taels of Raw Opium Have Been Secretly Shipped Out

Director Wen Hopes for Thorough Investigation

Since the discovery of the major case of Zhang Shaoyi, the director of the Third Section's Stolen Goods Department of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, stealing and exchanging raw opium, people in society have generally regarded it as an unprecedented scandal since the establishment of Shanghai police affairs, and most advocate a thorough investigation to clarify the truth of the case and avoid future shame for the police force. This reporter personally visited Director Wen and probed from various sources yesterday, and found that the case is unusually complex, involving many principal and accessory offenders. The details are described separately below.

▲Stolen Goods Warehouse Heavily Guarded. In recent months, the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team and various district branches have cracked down on a large number of opium cases, totaling about 30,000 to 40,000 taels. When each district team cracked the cases, they all used fire lacquer to seal them firmly, and added seals and stamps, and submitted them to the Third Section for preservation in the Stolen Goods Department, pending transfer to the municipal government for supervised destruction. Therefore, the department's responsibility is extremely important, and the prevention and control are also stricter. On weekdays, only the department director or section chief and other senior personnel can enter and exit to inspect the evidence. Other personnel in the bureau are generally not allowed to enter without authorization. In addition, if there is no stolen goods to be stored, the warehouse door is sealed and locked to ensure prudence. Therefore, whenever the director changes, the seat of the director of the Stolen Goods Department cannot be easily held by anyone other than the director's confidant or someone with close family ties.

▲Heavy Jute Bags Are Suspicious. Since Director Wen Yingxing took office at the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Zhang Shaoyi has succeeded as the director of the Stolen Goods Department. Zhang is young and mature, and has always been valued by Director Wen. Unexpectedly, there are things in the world that are beyond expectation. On the 28th of last month, at about 11:00 AM, while the police brigade in the bureau was patrolling around the bureau, a patrolling police officer Lin suddenly caught sight of the servants of the Stolen Goods Department, Ji Asi and Wu Deyi, and the servant of the Detective Team, Xiao Mazi, and others, carrying many heavy jute bags near the stolen goods warehouse, looking flustered and sneaky. At the same time, he saw two rickshaws parked there, seemingly waiting to transport the bags.

▲Switching Real Opium with Fake Opium. The police officers felt strange and stepped forward to examine them carefully. They saw two of the largest bags were full of real raw opium, worth nearly 10,000 yuan. There were also seven smaller bags, with the seal of the Water Patrol Team on them. Upon closer inspection, the bags were all fake opium (commonly known as "liao zi"). The police officers interrogated them, and Ji Asi claimed that he had been ordered by Director Zhang to switch the fake opium with the real opium. The police officers further asked where the fake opium came from. They replied that a certain team in the bureau had used cars to secretly transport them to the bureau in batches to switch with the real opium.

▲Zhang Shaoyi Ordered to Be Detained. Upon hearing this, the police officers felt even more shocked and immediately reported to the brigade commander and detained the three servants, waiting for the director to be notified the next morning. However, the next morning, after Director Zhang Shaoyi arrived at the bureau and heard the news, he immediately bailed out the three servants. At the same time, the brigade commander and Wu Ziquan, the director of the Third Section, also reported to the director based on the information they had. At that time, Director Wen questioned Zhang in detail. While he was thoroughly investigating, Mayor Wu Tiecheng had already heard about it and was extremely angry that such a major case had occurred in the Public Security Bureau. He immediately ordered Director Wen to first detain Zhang, question him, and report the details.

▲Secretary Han Involved in the Case. After receiving the order, Director Wen handed Zhang over to the brigade headquarters for detention and asked the Third Section to interrogate him. Two detailed interrogations have been conducted, but because the case involves secrets, it has not been allowed to be published. However, according to reliable information from the Judicial Section, during the first preliminary hearing, Zhang's confession involved many personnel in the bureau. During the second interrogation, the confession was revised. At this time, Zhang only claimed that the mastermind behind the case was Chief Secretary Han Jin (Zi Tuizhi), and claimed that Han had secretly discussed the switching of raw opium with him several times before the incident, but he had not agreed. Finally, he said that although someone had brought seven bags of fake opium to the bureau at that time, he still suspected that it was formal stolen goods.

▲Director Wen Issued a Statement. Yesterday afternoon, this reporter specially visited Director Wen, who said that Secretary Han had previously held important positions in the Jinghan, Jingfeng, Jingsui, and Jinpu Railways, and had a long-standing friendship with Yu (Wen referring to himself), and had never had any out-of-line behavior, and his personality was also quite noble. He had asked for three days of leave on the 28th of last month to return to his hometown of Hangzhou to sweep the tomb, and the leave had expired yesterday, but he had not yet canceled the leave. Today, he suddenly received a telegram from him, requesting to extend the leave. Regarding this matter, he had reported to Mayor Wu this morning, and the mayor ordered Han to be wanted. He has now telegraphed the Hangzhou Municipal Public Security Bureau to assist in finding and arresting him, and bringing him to justice for strict investigation. According to the law, he should be sent to the court for handling. Before Han is arrested, he will wait for the municipal government's orders to handle the matter. Today, detectives have been dispatched to the railway station and wharves to strictly monitor his whereabouts. Finally, Yu said that he knew the contents of this case very well, and that there must be special circumstances. Moreover, Secretary Han is nearly sixty years old, and is not very familiar with the situation in Shanghai. Even if it is to buy fake opium, those who are not experienced in this way will never be able to buy it. Just from this point alone, it is impossible for Han and Zhang to handle it alone. Yu hopes that this case will be thoroughly investigated so that Yu can show his honesty to society and gain the understanding of his superiors.

New Huangpu River Navigation Markers Established by the Jianghai Customs 107

Common Knowledge for Ships Navigating the Huangpu River

The tidal currents within the Huangpu River are very strong. In recent years, the number of merchant ships entering and leaving the port has gradually increased. In narrower sections of the river, merchant ships often collide and sink while turning around. This is often caused by sampans, barges, and small boats traversing the river without knowing how to avoid larger vessels, leading to capsizing accidents. News of drownings is heard almost daily. To maintain the safety of the Huangpu River, Mr. Gu Lien, Acting Director of the Port Authority, has specially revised various markers and issued a public notice to merchant ships in the port, instructing them on how to navigate and avoid accidents such as capsizing and falling into the water. New regulations have also been established regarding daytime and nighttime warning signs for dredgers and pump boats in the river, which are now being communicated to all ships, large and small, for compliance. Details are listed below:

▲ Warning Markers for Dredgers: There are many dredgers in the Huangpu River, dredging the riverbed and moored in various locations. The current regulations stipulate the flags, lights, and mooring symbols to be displayed: (1) A red flag and a solid black oblique square shape should be displayed to indicate that the dredger is moored in the middle of the Huangpu River. (2) A black sphere should be displayed to indicate that the dredger is moored closer to the Pudong side of the river. (3) Two black spheres should be displayed to indicate that the dredger is moored closer to the Shanghai side of the river. At night, warning signals should consist of a white light at both the bow and stern of the ship. (1) At night, three red lights arranged in a triangle, with one at the top and two at the bottom, should be displayed to indicate mooring in the middle of the Huangpu River. (2) Three red lights in a triangle, with a white light at the top and a red light at each end of the base line, should be displayed to indicate mooring closer to Pudong. (3) Three red lights in a triangle, with a red light at the apex and a white light at each end of the base line, should be displayed to indicate mooring closer to Shanghai.

▲ Warning Markers for Pump Boats: The warning markers for pump boats also stipulate that a red flag should be displayed during the day to indicate that the boat is connected to the riverbank with a hose. At night, three white lights should be displayed in a triangle, with the apex pointing upwards, to indicate that the boat is connected to the riverbank with a hose. All of the above-mentioned dredgers and pump boats must display these newly revised warning flags and lights when obstructing navigation in the Huangpu River. The lights used are quite powerful and can be seen from up to a mile away in clear weather. Yesterday, the Jianghai Customs Port Authority notified all shipping companies to distribute these new regulations regarding navigation markers in the Huangpu River to their ship personnel so that they can navigate the river with a clear basis and reduce unfortunate accidents.

Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau Streamlines Tax Collection 109

Xu Zhicheng, Director of the Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau, issued a proclamation yesterday, stating: "This is a proclamation regarding stamp tax, which is a good tax universally practiced worldwide and a legitimate source of national revenue. The original intent of implementing stamp tax was to have very low tax rates with broad application. All personnel certificates, once stamped in accordance with regulations, are recognized as legal evidence. Therefore, merchants and the public fulfill their obligation to pay national taxes and enjoy the right to protection under the law. If this can be understood by every household and universally applied, the burden on the people will be small, and the public revenue will gradually increase. This is beneficial to both the national economy and the people's livelihood. Shanghai is located in the central business district, where personnel matters are frequent and public awareness is high, surpassing other regions. In recent years, the sales volume of tax stamps has gradually increased. However, due to the vastness of the jurisdiction and the crisscrossing waterways, while the majority adhere to the regulations and diligently comply, there are still many instances of intentional evasion and disregard for the law. The Director of this Bureau is now under orders from the provincial bureau to urge stricter supervision and assessment. It is our duty to rectify tax collection. In addition to instructing sales personnel to comply and dispatching personnel for inspection at any time, we hereby issue this proclamation to all merchants and people transporting goods by land and water within our jurisdiction. All account books, receipts, permits, and licenses that require stamp duty must be handled in accordance with regulations and must not be evaded. In recent years, shops of various kinds often attempt to avoid stamp duty by not issuing invoices and using a type of informal note or slip that only lists the prices of goods without the year or the shop's stamp. Such cases have been discovered from time to time. This type of disguised invoice clearly constitutes illegal tax evasion, which greatly harms tax revenue. The Ministry of Finance previously issued a proclamation strictly prohibiting this practice. All shops selling goods worth one yuan or more must issue invoices and affix stamps in accordance with regulations. The use of disguised notes or delivery slips as substitutes, or the failure to affix stamps, is prohibited. Violators will be punished in accordance with the penalty provisions without leniency. This has been posted and announced in the past. We now urge all merchants to thoroughly eliminate all forms of tax evasion. For any goods worth one yuan or more, an invoice must be issued and stamped accordingly. Other documents such as receipts and settlement statements must not be replaced by letters or notices to avoid stamp duty. It should be understood that whether a business document violates regulations depends on its nature, not its form. Investigations and crackdowns will be based on documented evidence and will not allow for pretense. The Director of this Bureau understands the difficulties faced by merchants and is committed to balancing legal requirements with public concerns. We do not want anyone in our jurisdiction to mistakenly violate the penalty provisions due to opportunism. Therefore, we do not hesitate to provide prior warning. If the above-mentioned situations still occur in the future, once discovered or reported, we will only handle them in accordance with the law. Do not say that you were not warned in advance. Everyone must comply and not violate this proclamation."

No Results from Shanghai Social Bureau's Inquiry into Xu Chongdao Labor Dispute Yesterday 112

Workers Propose Six New Conditions

Over two hundred workers from ten branches of the Shanghai Xu Chongdao Chinese Medicine Store went on strike in support of their colleague Zheng Pei, who was allegedly falsely accused. The Shanghai Social Bureau convened an inquiry yesterday, but no results were achieved. The workers put forward six new conditions, while the management petitioned Party and government authorities. The details are as follows:

▲ Inquiry Results: Regarding the strike by all employees of Xu Chongdao Chinese Medicine headquarters and branches, the Municipal Social Bureau convened representatives from both labor and management at the Bureau at 10:00 AM yesterday for an inquiry. Those present included Zhang Meian, representative of the Chinese Medicine Trade Association; Fang Qingjian and Yuan Pinzhang, representatives of the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union; Cen Zhiliang, representative of Xu Chongdao's management; and Cen Yongkang and Sun Zhenkui, representatives of the labor side. The meeting was chaired by Mr. Wang, representative of the Social Bureau. First, representatives from both labor and management presented the details of the case. The Chairman then summarized the opinions of all parties and decided on two measures: (1) The report by Zheng Peiran, an employee of the seventh branch of the store, alleging that Qu Ming, the manager of the first branch, had falsely accused him of theft, involved personal disputes and fell within the scope of the judiciary, and should be resolved separately by Zheng and Qu through legal means. (2) The strike by the store's employees was sudden, and was not approved by Party and government authorities or permitted by the relevant higher-level union, and was therefore illegal. Therefore, all employees were advised to resume work as soon as possible. However, the labor side insisted on the dismissal of Qu Ming and refused to accept the previous measures, leading to a fruitless conclusion and dispersal.

▲ New Demands: At 2:00 PM yesterday, all employees of Xu Chongdao headquarters and branches held an emergency meeting. Cen Yongkang, the representative who attended the Social Bureau meeting, reported on the situation of the inquiry and proposed that the store be required to accept six new conditions: (1) Equal treatment for all employees within Xu Chongdao. (2) A uniform monthly wage increase of three yuan for all employees in all branches. (3) Apprentices who perform work should be treated as employees and should not work night shifts during their apprenticeship. (4) A uniform monthly wage of sixteen yuan for veteran employees. (5) Student subsidies: one yuan per month in the first year, two yuan per month in the second year, and three yuan per month in the third year. Bonuses: five yuan in the first year, ten yuan in the second year, and fifteen yuan in the third year. The minimum cost for meals should be 24 cents per table. (6) Restoration of the original holiday schedule: ten days for the Dragon Boat Festival, ten days for the Mid-Autumn Festival, and twenty days for the Lunar New Year.

▲ Management Petitions: At 3:00 PM yesterday, the store's manager Cen Zhiliang, accompanied by Zhang Meian, representative of the Chinese Medicine Trade Association, went to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Bureau to request a solution. Xu Yefu, Chief of the Third Section of the Social Bureau, received the representatives and stated that the Party and government authorities had decided on measures for handling the case after consultation and would implement them in the coming days. He asked the management to remain calm and await a legal resolution from the Bureau and the Party Headquarters. Subsequently, they went to the Municipal Party Headquarters, where they were received by Zhu Yangwu, Secretary of the Civil Training Section, who gave a similar response to that of the Social Bureau.

After the Suspension of the Shanghai South Public Bus Service 113

Workers Convened a General Meeting Yesterday to Discuss Solutions

Petition to Party and Government Authorities Scheduled for Today

Following the announcement of the suspension of operations by the Shanghai South Public Bus Company on Xie Xu Road, the company's outstanding wages, which the Party and government had already decided to pay, have been the subject of a dispute due to the company's insistence that workers return their uniforms, badges, and leave the factory. As a result, the outstanding wages have not yet been paid. The workers believe that the management lacks sincerity. In addition to seeking assistance from various sectors, they have decided that all workers will petition Party and government authorities this morning. The details are as follows:

▲ Outstanding Wages Unpaid: The issue of the company's outstanding wages had already been decided by the Party and government authorities, with both labor and management required to send representatives to verify the wage accounts before payment. However, other demands were to be dealt with separately. The management insisted that the workers agree to return their uniforms, badges, and leave the factory before the outstanding wages could be paid. The workers were willing to accept the issue of leaving the factory, but unanimously refused to return their uniforms and badges, as they were crucial for their livelihood. The company's outstanding wages have not yet been paid, and the dispute between the two sides is intensifying, raising concerns about the escalation of labor unrest.

▲ Workers' General Meeting: All the workers, noting that the directors and managers in charge of the company had been avoiding meetings and that only the liquidator, accountant Jiang Wanping, had been appearing to handle matters, deeply felt that there would be many obstacles to receiving the outstanding wages and that it would be even more difficult to realize their demands. Therefore, they had no choice but to plan for countermeasures. They convened a general meeting of all workers at 2:00 PM yesterday, and decided on the following: (1) Oppose the company's demand to return uniforms and badges. (2) All workers petition Party and government authorities, demanding that the company be ordered to resume operations. (3) The company should continue to pay wages during the suspension of operations. (4) If the company deliberately prolongs the situation and is unwilling to provide for the workers' livelihoods, they will fight with all their might to the death. (5) Appeal to all sectors to provide impartial assistance.

▲ Party and Government Mediation: Since the company announced the suspension of operations on August 30th, the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Bureau, after receiving reports from both labor and management, dispatched Fan Guoren and Peng Zhenqiu to investigate both sides and attempt to mediate. However, the workers demanded that outstanding wages be paid first, while the management insisted that the workers return their uniforms, badges, and leave the factory. Although these officials have been working hard to mediate for days and have drafted solutions, the situation has taken a turn for the worse, as both labor and management are taking extreme positions, making it even more difficult to resolve. According to Fan Guoren, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, they have drafted a solution and are proceeding step by step to resolve the labor unrest as soon as possible.

▲ Petition Today: All the workers, facing a precarious livelihood due to the suspension of operations and the non-payment of outstanding wages, and feeling that the company has no sincere intention to resolve the matter, decided at a general meeting to organize a team petition to Party and government authorities this morning, demanding that the company be ordered to resume operations.

Invention of Steel Type for Typewriters 124

Steel type was first invented in America, and then Japan modified it for use in Chinese typewriters. These were sold in our country, with an annual outflow of tens of thousands of dollars. Now, Mr. Yu Binqi, the inventor of the Chinese typewriter patented by the National Government, has succeeded through careful research due to the needs of his own machines and other typewriters. The type is suitable for all kinds of Chinese typewriters and remains unchanged after repeated use, truly a weapon of culture. In order to facilitate procurement from all sectors, a distribution office has been specially set up at the China Industrial Company, No. 9 Hankou Road, Shanghai. All are welcome to visit and test it.

Zhengda Bank Sues Huang Zhiqing et al. for Fraud 125

The Court Orders Out-of-Court Reconciliation

Saying Litigation Leads to Ruin

Zhengda Bank on Jiangxi Road recently commissioned lawyer Wu Guochang to file a complaint with the First Special Court of the Special District, accusing Huang Zhiqing, resident at No. 41 Xianmianci Road in Shanghai city, and Zou Jiabai, resident at No. 35 Gu Yuan Road in the French Concession, of the crime of fraudulently obtaining property by forging documents. The reasons for the prosecution are that Huang, in January of the 19th year, claimed that the Chongming Electric Power Co., Ltd., of which he was the chairman, was his own electric power plant. With Zou as guarantor, he borrowed 30,000 taels of standard silver. He drew up a mortgage loan agreement and a list of property, with items such as the factory building land license and insurance policy attached, with a promise to submit supplements later. He repeatedly delayed without submitting them, and failed to pay interest installments. Upon urging the guarantor, he said he would find a way to transfer the Chongming Electric Power Plant to settle the debt. Unexpectedly, there was no news afterwards. The court was forced to transfer the case to the Chongming County Government for prosecution. When shareholders of Chongming Electric Power Co., Ltd., such as Shi Yuming, came forward to file a principal intervention lawsuit, Huang admitted in court that it was a joint-stock company and that he had written "self-owned" because it was difficult to explain the debt at the time. Zou also hid and did not appear. In May of this year, the Chongming County Government ruled that the mortgage contract signed between Zhengda Bank and Huang Zhiqing, regarding all the property of Chongming Electric Power Co., Ltd., was invalid as collateral. Therefore, the defendants' behavior constituted two crimes under Articles 224 and 363 of the Criminal Law. This case was heard by Judge Fu Lin. Because the defendant claimed that Zhengda Bank was a legal entity, the chairman of the bank should come forward as the plaintiff so that he could bear the responsibility of the criminal lawsuit. If the complaint was inaccurate, a false accusation could be filed. Therefore, a responsible person had to sign his name. The plaintiff immediately added Wang Wenzhi, chairman of Zhengda Bank, and Zou Jiabai as the representative. The defendant argued that Zou was not the chairman, and according to the law, the chairman himself should be present in court. This point was still the focus of debate between the two sides at yesterday's hearing. Judge Pu advised Huang Zhiqing that the money he owed must eventually be repaid, and it would be better to reconcile out of court. Litigation leads to ruin. If reconciliation was not possible, Wang Wenzhi must be brought to court, and the hearing was adjourned to next Friday.

Wu Runsheng's Appeal to Confirm Identity in Inheritance Dispute Rejected 126

There was a Wu Meisheng, who had some property. He lived at No. 96 Xinzha Road. He married Lian, his first wife, who died early and left a son named Guoliang. His second wife, Bao, had no children. In April of this year, Wu died of illness. At that time, Guoliang attended to the funeral arrangements. Later, on May 21, Wu Runsheng, a distant nephew of Meisheng's clan (currently the Chinese manager of He Kang Foreign Firm on Beijing Road, i.e., the only son of Wu from the same township), sent a letter through lawyers Jiang Yiping and Zou Shengzu to Wu Bao, saying that Guoliang was not Meisheng's biological son but an adopted son. He claimed to be Meisheng's adopted son and opposed Guoliang's identity, severely questioning him and demanding the handover of property. As a result, Wu Bao hired lawyers Li Zuyu and Chen Ying to file a lawsuit with the Civil Division of the First Special Court against Wu Runsheng, requesting a judgment confirming that the defendant was not the adopted son of her late husband Wu Meisheng. The reason given was that Wu Runsheng was a distant nephew of Meisheng's clan and lived separately, having no connection with the plaintiff's family. During Wu Meisheng's mourning period, he sent elegiac couplets and tin foil paper items in the capacity of a clan nephew. The couplets even marked the relationship as uncle and nephew. Runsheng took the couplets away on the afternoon of May 19 under a pretext, which was removed by the doorman Xu Cheng, which could be proven. The defense of the defendant Wu Runsheng stated that Meisheng had no descendants, only an adopted son Guoliang. In the intercalary June of the 19th year, Guoliang had a daughter who celebrated her full month at the Yipinxiang Hotel. Wu Meisheng convened a meeting of relatives and decided that the defendant would inherit as a collateral heir, to continue the bloodline of the family. The relative Wu Xu could testify to this. However, the plaintiff did not notify the defendant of the mourning. He completely denied the plaintiff's claim of taking back the elegiac couplets and requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be rejected. The presiding judge Lou Ying ruled that Wu Runsheng was not the adopted son of the plaintiff's late husband Wu Meisheng. The litigation costs were to be borne by the defendant. Wu Runsheng refused to accept the judgment and hired the same three lawyers, Jiang Yiping, to appeal to the Second Branch of the High Court. Wu Bao also filed a defense, requesting that the original judgment be upheld and the appeal be rejected. The Second Branch of the High Court concluded the hearing and, at 3:00 PM yesterday, the Chief Judge of the Civil Division, Hu Yigu, convened a collegial panel to announce the judgment. The main text stated: The appeal is dismissed, and the litigation costs of the second instance are to be borne by the appellant.

Zhejiang Bandits Bring Guns to Shanghai to Plot Illegal Activities 127

Wang Chonghao, a Chinese detective from the Hongkou Police Station, arrested Xu Jia Kui, an Anhui native, at No. 56 Taopeng Road at 1:10 AM on the 19th of last month. He also confiscated a pistol and four bullets. Subsequently, he apprehended three other fellow villagers, Wu Yeming, Zhu Yeyu, and Yuan Peicai, in a teahouse near the Pingliang Road vegetable market. They were all sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong continued the hearing in the Fourth Criminal Court. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's lawyer, stated that the second defendant, Wu Yeming, had previously committed a kidnapping case in the Tianran River area of Zhujing, Deqing County, Zhejiang. The local water police had arrested three suspects, and Wu was one of them. He later escaped to Shanghai. However, the firearms and ammunition were handed over to Xu Jia Kui with the intention of committing robbery in Shanghai again, hoping that his accomplices could share the ransom after it was paid. The police station is prosecuting the four defendants under the Military Firearms Control Regulations and requested the court to handle the case according to the law. Today, Gu Liancheng, an investigator from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, arrived and requested a transfer. The police station did not object but required a formal announcement. According to Detective Gu's statement, the Deqing County Government in Zhejiang had sent a letter of notification. When questioned, Yu Jia Kui confessed that the pistol was indeed brought by Wu Yeming and given to him, but he knew nothing about Wu's kidnapping case in the interior. Wu Yeming denied participating in the kidnapping case in the interior. He admitted that he brought the pistol to Shanghai and gave it to Xu Jia Kui, but he did not intend to commit illegal activities in Shanghai. Zhu Yeyu and Yuan Peicai stated that they had just met Wu and knew nothing else. Judge Shen concluded the debate on the case and scheduled a pronouncement. The defendants were returned to custody.

Losing His Life for Renting a Bicycle 128

Accomplice Liu Xigen Arrested

Zhou Dianchen, a 36-year-old native of Xuzhou, lived at No. 39 Xinshunli, Yangshupu Road. At about 10:00 AM on the 31st of last month, he went to the Jixing Bicycle Shop at No. 8 on the same road to rent a bicycle and had a disagreement with the shop's apprentice, slapping the apprentice in the face. At 8:20 PM that evening, the shop owner, Ji Youdao, gathered several people and went to the vicinity of Xinshunli to reason with Zhou. They disagreed and started fighting. As a result, Zhou was stabbed in the leg and fell to the ground. A patrolling police officer arrived and arrested the people involved in the fight, who all fled. The injured Zhou was taken to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment but died of his injuries at 6:00 AM the next morning. The body was sent to the Forensic Examination Office on Feilun Road for examination. Subsequently, the police arrested Liu Xigen, an accomplice from Wuxi, and detained him at the Yangshupu Police Station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Fourth Criminal Court of the First Special District. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's lawyer, stated the case. Ms. Zhu Xu, a woman from Ningbo, testified that the deceased was her foster father and that she had witnessed the defendant's complicity at the scene. Zhu Cailin stated that he heard a fight and went to mediate but was pushed into the river. When he got up, Zhou Dianchen had already been beaten and injured and was being sent to the hospital. When questioned, the defendant confessed that he also went to mediate and did not beat Zhou, which the employees of the Zhengmao Clothing Store and Liu Mao's Bicycle Shop nearby could testify to. He asked for verification. Judge Shen Bingrong adjourned the hearing to re-examine the evidence. At about 10:00 AM, a prosecutor from the court went to the site and examined Zhou Dianchen's body, ordering the family to claim the body for coffining and burial. Liu Xigen was returned to the police station for custody.

Continental Daily's Reactionary Opinions 129

The Printer Suffers as a Result

Tang Bao, an inspector from the Public Security Bureau, was ordered on the morning of the 23rd of last month to forward a notice to the Old Gate Police Station to dispatch detectives to assist in searching No. 352 Fusenli, Beihai Road, for printing reactionary newspapers. At that time, the printing house was printing the Continental Daily. The staff members Qian Jingao and Yang Enpei were arrested. The next day, the police station applied to the Second Branch of the High Court for their detention. Yesterday was the date for the trial of this case. Tang Bao, an inspector from the Public Security Bureau, stated that the Public Security Bureau had received a telegram from the Central Government and Chairman Liu of Henan, stating that Wang Aoxi was running the Continental Daily in Shanghai and that its opinions were close to being reactionary. He was asked to arrest him. So, at 3:00 AM on the 23rd, he went to the China Commercial Printing Company, which was printing the newspaper, to search and arrest. Thirty copies of the Continental Daily had already been printed, and the two staff members Qian Jingao and Yang Enpei were arrested. At the same time, 7,000 copies of the old Continental Daily were found in No. 180 Funingli, Zhejiang Road. He requested to be transferred to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Qian Jingao stated that the printing of the Continental Daily was introduced by the Dajing Newspaper House and the Dajing Printing House. The printing contract was witnessed by the famous lawyers Li and Liu, and the legal advisors of the Continental Daily were also Li and Liu. Moreover, the distribution of the newspaper was public. He really did not know it was reactionary. The contract for printing this newspaper could prove that he did not know the situation. The police station's lawyer stated that Qian and Gao were not principal offenders, and the crime of printing reactionary newspapers occurred in the Public Concession. Therefore, the police station opposed the transfer and believed that the Second Branch of the High Court should try the case. Since the defendant claimed that there was a contract to prove his innocence, he should be ordered to produce the contract for review. The Presiding Judge Yu Ye ordered the 7,000 copies of the newspaper found on Zhejiang Road to be taken away by the Public Security Bureau and ordered Qian Jingao to go home to retrieve the contract and submit it to the court for further review.

Fire on Arrabastor Road 130

No. 19 Jinheli, Arrabastor Road, Public Concession, suddenly caught fire at 3:00 AM yesterday. Black smoke immediately filled the air, and the fire was unstoppable. It spread to No. 21. The Fire Brigade rushed to the scene and tried their best to put out the fire. It was extinguished in over an hour. Afterwards, a total of three houses were burned down, with losses estimated at over 1,000 yuan.

Letter 143

To the esteemed editor,

We have reviewed the news article published in your newspaper yesterday entitled [Shanghai South Public Bus Company Pays Back Wages After Shutdown]. There is no such provision in item 3 of the alternative solutions [Workers leave the factory after receiving payment]. The party and government agencies convened both parties on the day before yesterday (September 1) to resolve the issue of wage arrears independently. Although the capital side proposed returning the uniforms and badges at that time, the workers immediately declared that if the company reclaimed the uniforms, badges, and workers leaving the factory, all other conditions must be resolved before that could happen. In the stalemate, Peng Zhenqiu of the Social Affairs Bureau ordered that the back wages be paid first, and other issues be mediated in another case. Therefore, the statement that workers left the factory after receiving payment is completely inconsistent with the facts. Therefore, we request that it be corrected as soon as possible.

Sincerely,

Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai South Public Bus Workers' Union

September 2
